  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8cf5cad5-be50-48c0-8401-4dd7942213ba'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer10268414493618567660">Newly-orphaned Anne Beddingfeld is a nice English girl looking for a bit of adventure in London. But she stumbles upon more than she bargained for! Anne is on the platform at Hyde Park Corner tube station when a man falls onto the live track, dying instantly. A doctor examines the man, pronounces him dead, and leaves, dropping a note on his way.   <span id="freeText10268414493618567660" style="display:none">Newly-orphaned Anne Beddingfeld is a nice English girl looking for a bit of adventure in London. But she stumbles upon more than she bargained for! Anne is on the platform at Hyde Park Corner tube station when a man falls onto the live track, dying instantly. A doctor examines the man, pronounces him dead, and leaves, dropping a note on his way. Anne picks up the note, which reads "17.1 22 Kilmorden Castle". The next day the newspapers report that a beautiful ballet dancer has been found dead there-- brutally strangled. A fabulous fortune in diamonds has vanished. And now, aboard the luxury liner Kilmorden Castle, mysterious strangers pillage her cabin and try to strangle her. What are they looking for? Why should they want her dead? Lovely Anne is the last person on earth suited to solve this mystery... and the only one who can! Anne's journey to unravel the mystery takes her as far afield as Africa and the tension mounts with every step... and Anne finds herself struggling to unmask a faceless killer known only as 'The Colonel'....</span>
  <a data-text-id="10268414493618567660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4281864477077574123">The Man in the Brown Suit (Colonel Race #1), Agatha Christie<br/><br/>The Man in the Brown Suit is a work of detective fiction by Agatha Christie, first published in the UK by The Bodley Head on 22 August 1924 and in the US by Dodd, Mead and Company later in the same year. <br/><br/>Orphan Anne Beddingfeld, in search of adventure, follows the clue in a note from the pocket of a murder victim. Her journey takes her on an ocean voyage from London to Africa, and finally to a lost island, on the trail of stolen diamond</span>
  <span id="freeText4281864477077574123" style="display:none">The Man in the Brown Suit (Colonel Race #1), Agatha Christie<br /><br />The Man in the Brown Suit is a work of detective fiction by Agatha Christie, first published in the UK by The Bodley Head on 22 August 1924 and in the US by Dodd, Mead and Company later in the same year. <br /><br />Orphan Anne Beddingfeld, in search of adventure, follows the clue in a note from the pocket of a murder victim. Her journey takes her on an ocean voyage from London to Africa, and finally to a lost island, on the trail of stolen diamonds. <br /><br />Nadina, a "Russian" dancer, receives a visit in her dressing room from Count Sergius Paulovitch. Both are in the service of a man they call "the Colonel", an international agent provocateur and criminal. After many years, "the Colonel" is retiring, leaving his agents high and dry. Nadina has double-crossed the Colonel, however, keeping some De Beers diamonds from a crime years before. She now plans to blackmail the Colonel with the diamonds.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 2008 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: مردی با لباس قهوه‌ ای؛ نویسنده: آگاتا کریستی؛ مترجم: محمدعلی ایزدی؛ تهران، کارآگاه، 1385؛ در 362ص؛ <br /><br />زندگی دختر جوانی، به نام «آنی»، پس از مرگ پدرش، که مردم‌شناس معروفی بوده، با مشکل مواجه می‌شود.«آنی» از لحاظ مالی، با تنگنای شدیدی روبرو شده.آقای بدینگ‌فلد وکیل سابق، نامه ی محبت‌آمیزی به آنی، می‌نویسد، و اعلام می‌کند که «حاضر است به او مسکن مجانی بدهد»، ولی آنی مایل نیست پیشنهاد را بپذیرد.او تصمیم دارد دور دنیا را بگردد، و زندگی پرماجرایی در پیش گیرد.«آنی» در ایستگاه مترو، مرد ریزنقشی را میببیند که ناگهان روی ریلها افتاد، و دچار برق‌گرفتگی شد.سپس مردی با لباس قهوه‌ ای، راهش را از میان جمعیت، باز می‌کند، و خود را بالای سر قربانی می‌رساند، و اعلام می‌کند که آن مرد فوت کرده است.سپس با عجله دور می‌شود، و تکه کاغذی از خود بر جای می‌گذارد، که روی آن نوشته «قلعه کیلموردن، 122-17»؛ ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_2194134186" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194134186" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194134186?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Christie thrillers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=abandoned-without-prejudice">abandoned-without-prejudice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=classic">classic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194134186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11020625057736385402">In the spirit of Read All the Christies, I ordered this after seeing it in someone's feed. Could have been my mood, but I found that it didn't sustain my interest. I've been reading Christie for a <i>long</i> time, so it's not like I opened it with expectations of heart-pumping action. I'd say I gave the first seventy or so pages a solid effort, but it never really caught me. <br/><br/>Part of it was definitely as Miriam noted in her review, that of connection with the lead, a young woman who wants 'adventure.' </span>
  <span id="freeText11020625057736385402" style="display:none">In the spirit of Read All the Christies, I ordered this after seeing it in someone's feed. Could have been my mood, but I found that it didn't sustain my interest. I've been reading Christie for a <i>long</i> time, so it's not like I opened it with expectations of heart-pumping action. I'd say I gave the first seventy or so pages a solid effort, but it never really caught me. <br /><br />Part of it was definitely as Miriam noted in her review, that of connection with the lead, a young woman who wants 'adventure.' After witnessing a man collapse on the railway, and another man claiming to be a doctor rifle through the dead man's pockets, she manages to involve herself in investigating the death. It's quite vague, and she needs to become a journalist in order to get access to information. She's quite plucky, and it all feels very modern for a period book. It's got that early Katharine Hepburn feel to it.<br /><br />I skimmed; there's eventually African adventure, romance, and apparently espionage, which explains it. Christie's thrillers have never particularly worked for me. It makes even more sense when I see in a friend's review that this was written as a serial, which means it was a very different set-up than the normal story. Apparently, isolated country manors and long train rides are where it is at for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11020625057736385402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2050470254045025524" style="display:none">The first in the Colonel Race series, the story began on an intriguing note with a very cryptic discussion about double crossing a spy. We then flip to meeting Anne Bedingfield who becomes involved in the intrigue after witnessing an incident that could be tied to a recent murder. Soon Anne is on a ship bound for South Africa with a host of different characters. One of them being Colonel Race and the other being Sir Eustace Pedler whose diary entries break up Anne's narrative.<br /><br />This was a <b> slow burn </b> that definitely bored me to tears. Colonel Race didn't really emerge as a character of interest and I didn't like the general way that AC worked the narrative.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153520219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1018505776681028643">4.5 Stars - If it weren't for the elements that get introduced later in the story that require serious CWs for colonialism, racial stereotypes, & intimations of intimate partner violence, I'd have given this the full 5 stars. This book just rang all the bells for me of what I love in a Christie... great tone, memorable characters, fun mystery plot, and strong evocation of time/place. This is the best action adventure type mystery I've read from Christie. I wish the "of its time" elements weren't</span>
  <span id="freeText1018505776681028643" style="display:none">4.5 Stars - If it weren't for the elements that get introduced later in the story that require serious CWs for colonialism, racial stereotypes, &amp; intimations of intimate partner violence, I'd have given this the full 5 stars. This book just rang all the bells for me of what I love in a Christie... great tone, memorable characters, fun mystery plot, and strong evocation of time/place. This is the best action adventure type mystery I've read from Christie. I wish the "of its time" elements weren't there, because they really do dampen the shine of an otherwise sparkly book full of fun- they take me out of the book and make me put on my "analyzing this as a historical artifact of a different time" hat on rather than just my "rompy good time" hat.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2104226105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2104226105" />
    <a title="emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58877035-emily"><img alt="emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587215502p2/58877035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2104226105?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emily" href="/user/show/58877035-emily">emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2104226105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3740954707041519520"><i>It is really a hard life. Men will not be nice to you if you are not good-looking, and women will not be nice to you if you are.</i><br/><br/>My first encounter with Agathie Christie's work was not a disappointment - although, perhaps, it is not one of her most popular books, it was certainly an enjoyable entry into this genre. <br/><br/>Think Africa and diamonds and adventure and mystery - welcome to 'The Man in The Brown Suit'. <br/><br/>What I liked: <br/><br/>✔︎-<b>The fact that it was set in South Africa.</b> Everybody's heard the famous sa</span>
  <span id="freeText3740954707041519520" style="display:none"><i>It is really a hard life. Men will not be nice to you if you are not good-looking, and women will not be nice to you if you are.</i><br /><br />My first encounter with Agathie Christie's work was not a disappointment - although, perhaps, it is not one of her most popular books, it was certainly an enjoyable entry into this genre. <br /><br />Think Africa and diamonds and adventure and mystery - welcome to 'The Man in The Brown Suit'. <br /><br />What I liked: <br /><br />✔︎-<b>The fact that it was set in South Africa.</b> Everybody's heard the famous saying that <b>books allow the mind to travel and see what the eyes would normally not be able to.</b> The hot, African climate and culture were huge assets of this book, creating a very intriguing backdrop to this mystery novel, and although some color connotations of the word 'murder mystery' might be black and grey, maybe darker browns or even white - this book put a complete twist to that stereotype. It was <b>packed with colour and scenery</b> (not too many descriptions), to create a vivid and entertaining read. <br /><br />✔︎-<b>The travelling aspect</b>. Like I mentioned previously, the setting in this book is marvelous. To be very blunt and save you from needless spoilers, let me just highlight the fact that there will be scenes in <b>London</b>; there will be <b>cruises</b>; and <b>train rides</b> and <b>exploring waterfalls</b>. That's enough you need to know. <br /><br />✔︎-<b>The friendships (and romance)</b> At one point, in this book our protagonist, Anne Beddingfield, meets a new acquaintance, and <b>their friendship slowly develops over time into true companionship.</b> Also, for those who like a little romance, there is definitely some present. It felt a little 'cheesy' at times, but sometimes, a little extra cheese is what you need. Their relationship was, to put, a little casually, <b>very cute</b>, although maybe it was a bit too much at times (especially when Anne immediately fell in love, claiming she loves him and wants to spend her life with him, when she literally just let him a couple of minutes ago, but still, it was heartwarming). <br /><br />✔︎-<b>The actual mystery and murderer.</b> Don't threat, I won't spoil the ending for you, but let me just point out, that it was extremely <b>well thought out</b> (cheeky little rhyme there), and nothing is as it seems to be. <br /><br />✔︎-<b>There were references to things Christie experienced herself.</b> I read a very interesting blog on wordpress (SPOILERS: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.google.pl/amp/s/knowingchristie.wordpress.com/2013/05/17/notes-on-the-man-in-the-brown-suit/amp/">https://www.google.pl/amp/s/knowingch...</a>) that claimed that some of the characters might have been based on people she met, and there was a particular scene (the one with stray cats) that was loosely based of the time where she had attempted to rescue a dog. <br /><br />✔︎-<b>Two points of views.</b> This kept the book fast paced and <b>very misleading</b>, although Pedler was extremely sexist and sarcastic - his diary entries were interesting to read, and he was a little hilariously pathetic at times. <br /><br />The only problem with this book was that: <br /><br />✘- I, at times, found myself very irritated with Anne and, although, I admit to <b>her being very brace and intelligent</b> - her actions didn't always <b>do her wits justice.</b> Some of her decisions were a little immature, and if not for one special person, I doubt she'd be alive at the end of the novel. <br /><br /><br />✘- <b>Also, I found myself a little lost with all the clues</b>, but that might be because I am very inexperienced with this genre, and just need to pay more attention. A reread might be in order, although I'm not a big fan of re-reading books. <br /><br />Overall, my first experience with an Agathe Christie book was a success. Hopefully, I'll be able to read more soon. Murder on the Orient Express, anyone?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3740954707041519520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826393945?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/31554347-the-man-in-the-brown-suit">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone!</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826393945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12064090720351167006">Before there was Miss Jane Marple and very shortly after the birth of Hercule Poirot, there was Anne Beddingfield, the plucky heroine of <i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i>. Dame Agatha Christie included Hercule Poirot in 45 books and Miss Jane Marple in more than a dozen. Even Tommy and Tuppence Beresford appear in four novels and a collection of short stories. But Jane Beddingfield appears only in <i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i> (although another character in this novel, the debonair Colonel Race, went on to </span>
  <span id="freeText12064090720351167006" style="display:none">Before there was Miss Jane Marple and very shortly after the birth of Hercule Poirot, there was Anne Beddingfield, the plucky heroine of <i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i>. Dame Agatha Christie included Hercule Poirot in 45 books and Miss Jane Marple in more than a dozen. Even Tommy and Tuppence Beresford appear in four novels and a collection of short stories. But Jane Beddingfield appears only in <i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i> (although another character in this novel, the debonair Colonel Race, went on to appear in three more). More’s the pity! I would trade Tuppence Beresford and three dozen more heroines for Anne any day of the week, and how wonderful it would be to have a dozen Anne Beddingfield novels to read!<br /><br />Anne Beddingfield, the daughter of a famous but impecunious archeologist, dreams of a life of adventure right out of the Rhodesian romance novels and the cliffhanger film series <i>The Perils of Pamela</i> she adores. On her father’s death, the intrepid orphan is so anxious for adventure that she casts caution to the wind after witnessing the death of one L.B. Carton at the Hyde Park Tube Station. Anne spends her last £86 to travel on the ship <i>Kilmorden Castle</i> to continue her investigation into both Carton’s murder and a related one. Onboard ship, Anne gets enough excitement to satisfy anyone — including any reader lucky enough to get a hold of this book. I know it’s a cliché, but Anne really <i>is</i> plucky, clever, and imaginative, and I fell in love with her immediately. I only wish I could enjoy her in some sequels. Highly, highly recommended.<br /><br />Narrator Emilia Fox on the Audible edition of <i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i> makes the tale even more sublime.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12064090720351167006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6475320402876662368">4.5*<br/><br/><i>“I had the firm conviction that, if I went about looking for adventure, adventure would meet me halfway. It is a theory of mine that one always gets what one wants.”</i><br/><br/><i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i>, or <i>Anna the Adventurous</i>, was published as a serial in 1923, and is completely over the top!   <span id="freeText6475320402876662368" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><br /><i>“I had the firm conviction that, if I went about looking for adventure, adventure would meet me halfway. It is a theory of mine that one always gets what one wants.”</i><br /><br /><i>The Man in the Brown Suit</i>, or <i>Anna the Adventurous</i>, was published as a serial in 1923, and is completely over the top! Instead of our ‘usual’ detective story, we have a thriller, involving an international crime organisation with a secret arch-villain at its head, although there is of course murder and mystery. All starts with our intrepid heroine witnessing a man fall to his death at Hyde Park station. Add to this a piece of paper with a cryptic clue, the smell of mothballs, and a man in a brown suit, and our Anna throws herself to the chase, leading her into ever more dangerous situation, and a trip to South Africa!!<br /><br />You do still get Christie’s sarcastic self through the lines, with the wicked wit shining through the descriptions and narration, but this is ultimately ‘just’ a fun adventure. Don’t over think it - just enjoy it, like I did :0)</span>

<div id="review_1248138175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1248138175" />
    <a title="F.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1309606-f-r"><img alt="F.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544886612p2/1309606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248138175?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="F.R." href="/user/show/1309606-f-r">F.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248138175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5556557474368970938">Forget the mystery, forget the complex scheme hatched by a mysterious criminal mastermind, Agatha Christie’s ‘The Man in the Brown Suit’ is really a spoof. Written in 1924 it has the suspense serial, the kind with feisty, flapper heroines at their centre, directly in its sights. But hang on, it's more than that: this was actually written in serialised form as ‘Anne the Adventuress’ and so right from the off it is both satirising the over the top adventure story whilst wholeheartedly being one.<br/><br/>We</span>
  <span id="freeText5556557474368970938" style="display:none">Forget the mystery, forget the complex scheme hatched by a mysterious criminal mastermind, Agatha Christie’s ‘The Man in the Brown Suit’ is really a spoof. Written in 1924 it has the suspense serial, the kind with feisty, flapper heroines at their centre, directly in its sights. But hang on, it's more than that: this was actually written in serialised form as ‘Anne the Adventuress’ and so right from the off it is both satirising the over the top adventure story whilst wholeheartedly being one.<br /><br />We have here Anne Beddingfield, a recently orphaned, beautiful young woman, who craves adventure. On witnessing a mysterious death at a tube station, she throws herself impulsively into the mystery and before long is sailing to South Africa on the trail of a mysterious criminal mastermind. Peril is never far away for feisty Anne: she is nearly strangled aboard ship, kidnapped by a fake museum curator, and – most incredibly – lured into walking off the side of a ravine. But the indomitable spirit of this courageous Miss can’t be stopped, and she’s back on the trail as tenacious as ever.<br /><br />This is looser, fresher, funnier Christie than is the norm. It helps that the book half acknowledges that its heroine is a tad dim (if she, and her friends, had a better memory for faces the mystery would be over much sooner), and the result is triumphantly a novel that spoofs the genre, whilst buying into it completely and celebrating it. The mystery falls into the background as we follow Anne through one scrape after another, relishing her ability to regain her poise after every mis-step, whilst wondering at just how it is she makes so many glaring mistakes.<br /><br />Obviously this being Christie it’s a book locked into the English class structure and the value of colonialism; there are also some views on marriage that might raise a few eyebrows, whilst the assertion at the end that the main victim was <i>“the kind of woman who deserved to die”</i> does seem a bit harsh after the light soufflé of a book which has gone before. But this is a fine self-aware adventure, which knows it’s being absurd even as it’s taking itself seriously, and is without a doubt the most fun I have ever had with Dame Agatha.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5556557474368970938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2205751659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2205751659" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8575414-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441431450p2/8575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2205751659?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2205751659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2611654920513210521">My first Christie without Poirot or Marple and I still enjoyed it, much to my surprise. Anne was a feisty, independent minded protagonist. She was a bit of an insta detective though. A good range of supporting characters. It was also interesting to read about South Africa and Rhodesia: contemporary fiction at the time, and now historical fiction. <br/>You wouldn’t know that this is one of Christie’s earlier novels.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Charles  van Buren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47208326-charles-van-buren"><img alt="Charles  van Buren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555275074p2/47208326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3189368949?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charles  van Buren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charles  van Buren" href="/user/show/47208326-charles-van-buren">Charles  van Buren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/48743085-the-man-in-the-brown-suit-amazonclassics-edition">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3189368949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6646149398087649461"><strong>Below average Agatha Christie</strong><br/><br/>Review of Kindle edition<br/>Publication date: January 2, 2020Publisher: AmazonClassics<br/>Language: English<br/>ASIN: B07ZH6HD1M<br/>Amazon.com Sales Rank: 1552<br/>271 pages<br/><br/>This early Agatha Christie novel was published in 1924 between the introductions of Hercule Poirot and Miss Marple. It reads as though Christie had not yet hit her stride as a mature mystery author. In fact THE MAN IN THE BROWN SUIT is not strictly a mystery. Instead, it is a rather tame adventure/thriller/romance nove</span>
  <span id="freeText6646149398087649461" style="display:none"><strong>Below average Agatha Christie</strong><br /><br />Review of Kindle edition<br />Publication date: January 2, 2020Publisher: AmazonClassics<br />Language: English<br />ASIN: B07ZH6HD1M<br />Amazon.com Sales Rank: 1552<br />271 pages<br /><br />This early Agatha Christie novel was published in 1924 between the introductions of Hercule Poirot and Miss Marple. It reads as though Christie had not yet hit her stride as a mature mystery author. In fact THE MAN IN THE BROWN SUIT is not strictly a mystery. Instead, it is a rather tame adventure/thriller/romance novel centered around a mystery.<br /><br />Near the beginning, the future sleuth/adventurer, Anne Beddingfeld engages in a bit of introspective wishful thinking. One of the things she thinks of is the cinematic exploits of Pamela in the movie serial, THE PERILS OF PAMELA: "There was the cinema too, with a weekly episode of “The Perils of Pamela.” Pamela was a magnificent young woman. Nothing daunted her. She fell out of aeroplanes, adventured in submarines, climbed skyscrapers and crept about in the Underworld without turning a hair. She was not really clever, The Master Criminal of the Underworld caught her each time, but as he seemed loath to knock her on the head in a simple way, and always doomed her to death in a sewer gas chamber or by some new and marvellous means, the hero was always able to rescue her at the beginning of the following week’s episode." This quote pretty well sums up this novel. A literary movie serial with a game, enthusiastic young woman who is not quite competent but is very lucky. I read to about 60% through and realized that I didn't care who did what.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6646149398087649461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But adventure finds her when a strange-smelling man falls off an Underground platform and is electrocuted on the rails. The police verdict is accidental death. But who was the man in the brown suit who examined the body before running away? Armed with only one cryptic clue, Anne is determined to track him down and bring the mysterious killer to justice.<br /><br />Drafted and partly inspired by the Christies' Grand Tour of the British Commonwealth, The Man in the Brown Suit was written in her flat in Earl's Court with Agatha Christie evoking exotic African landscapes from memory.<br /><br />The story features an appearance from Secret Service agent Colonel Race who assists the heroine, and would appear in three further novels: 'Cards on the Table', 'Death on the Nile' and 'Sparkling Cyanide'. <br /><br />Published in 1924 by 'The Bodley Head', the novel was first serialised in 'The Evening News' under the title 'Anna, the Adventurous'.<br /><br />Did you know?<br />The £500 Agatha Christie received for the first publication of this story paid for her first car - a grey bottle-nosed Morris Cowley."</span>

    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1242515-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346493023p2/1242515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60420309?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/1242515-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1242515-hannah?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60420309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10895391796671092944">A great read. As always, Christie is a master of the crime/detective genre, managing to make this a fun and exciting romp without decreasing any of the mystery and sense of the sinister. <br/><br/>All of the characters had their own charms, but Colonel Race really made the book, even though he seemed to stay in the backdrop a lot of the time. I must say I felt rather sorry for his lack of luck with Anne, but I'm looking forward to revisiting his character in the later books. Anne, although not the most li</span>
  <span id="freeText10895391796671092944" style="display:none">A great read. As always, Christie is a master of the crime/detective genre, managing to make this a fun and exciting romp without decreasing any of the mystery and sense of the sinister. <br /><br />All of the characters had their own charms, but Colonel Race really made the book, even though he seemed to stay in the backdrop a lot of the time. I must say I felt rather sorry for his lack of luck with Anne, but I'm looking forward to revisiting his character in the later books. Anne, although not the most likeable heroine, is spunky and fearless, and her romance with Harry is one of the highlights of this book. There's always something attractive about a brave and pretty young lady on an adventure falling in love with a handsome, rugged young man who's been framed for murder. Christie turns this tired old cliche into something that holds your interest and makes you want to turn the page.<br /><br />The Man in the Brown Suit is a must-read for all Christie fans, and those who fancy a fast and furious bit of reading fun. There's a little of something in it for everyone; a crime (and its solving), unique characters, a spot of romance, and an all-round adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10895391796671092944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435972476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1710490391782208397">A great thriller from Christie's earlier writings. Published in 1924, it has traces of the Western world's racial bias against the Africans. The only disappointment is that published just a year after Poirot's great thriller- The Murder on the Links, Christie decided to give him a miss. However overall the pace is racy and you get a good ringside view of South African terrain.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2469711508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469711508" />
    <a title="Ken" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38999260-ken"><img alt="Ken" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446483502p2/38999260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2469711508?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken" href="/user/show/38999260-ken">Ken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2469711508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2019975375282578437">One of Christie’s earlier novels. <br/>Just like most of her stories during the early 1920’s, this is more of an adventure thriller than the traditional Whodunnit that you’d associate with her.<br/><br/>Young Anne Beddingfeld is looking for adventure, when she witnesses what seems to appear as an accidental death on the London Underground it soon leads her travelling to South Africa.<br/><br/>I really loved the set up of this novel, it felt so familiar to many of Christie’s other novels. I was instantly hooked on the my</span>
  <span id="freeText2019975375282578437" style="display:none">One of Christie’s earlier novels. <br />Just like most of her stories during the early 1920’s, this is more of an adventure thriller than the traditional Whodunnit that you’d associate with her.<br /><br />Young Anne Beddingfeld is looking for adventure, when she witnesses what seems to appear as an accidental death on the London Underground it soon leads her travelling to South Africa.<br /><br />I really loved the set up of this novel, it felt so familiar to many of Christie’s other novels. I was instantly hooked on the mystery.<br />Even the journey to South Africa had some great intriguing moments.<br /><br />The majority of the story is told through Anne’s perspective, she’s such an interesting character and was easy to follow her story.<br />During the second half of the novel the story starts to introduce diary entries which I found to be slightly jarring and disrupted the flow of the story.<br /><br />Even though I probably won’t recommend this to a Christie novice as an introductory point, I still felt it was the best one out of all her early thrillers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2019975375282578437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2337872001?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337872001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3555947271574266157">In the early 1990's I was first introduced to Agatha Christie's novels and was quickly drawn into her stories. Before the days of Amazon and Kindles, I would enjoy a visit to the local bookstore and find if they had any new to me Agatha paperbacks. I read a good number but that was limited to availability, so many like this story I had never read. Life became busy and my reading dropped off until my Kindle days started but even though I had many Christie kindle books, I only have read a handful </span>
  <span id="freeText3555947271574266157" style="display:none">In the early 1990's I was first introduced to Agatha Christie's novels and was quickly drawn into her stories. Before the days of Amazon and Kindles, I would enjoy a visit to the local bookstore and find if they had any new to me Agatha paperbacks. I read a good number but that was limited to availability, so many like this story I had never read. Life became busy and my reading dropped off until my Kindle days started but even though I had many Christie kindle books, I only have read a handful which I enjoyed but my LOVE for her novels is back after reading "The Man in the Brown Suit"!!! An Goodreads friend (Radwa)[Thanks you!!! :)] suggested "Sparkling Cyanide",which I was about to start reading until I came on the page that stated this was book 1 of a series, so I decided to read this and then follow up with book 4- "Sparkling Cyanide" . I decided to read books 2 &amp; 3 when I read Hercule Poirot series because they are part of that series too, so I leave it till then. <br />I always find it interesting how books "drop in our laps", meaning how a book is choosen over others to be read next. Enough of that...<br />I loved this story from the get go and was wondering throughout what the mysteries were and how Christie would play this out. I remember being always surprised when I was younger and being older now, she still surprised me with her twists but living life I could see somethings coming I would not think possible in my youth but still quite not sure given how it was played out or if it would go that direction. Up to the very last she shocked me with her twists. I loved it!! I also don't remember Christie being so humorous that I was laughing inwardly to her word play. If you like adventure, romance, murder mystery and other mysteries, then this book is a perfectly wonderful read for you! <br />In brief the story, right after Anne's father dies this orphan girl finds herself involved in a mysterious caper of sorts which has intrigue at every corner.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6182875393021558930">What a hoot this is! It’s so melodramatic and the storyline is quite absurd but it was just what I needed to lighten my mood. Anne Beddingfeld is a pompous, self righteous, impressionable and bored young woman. Having lost her father recently, she spends her entire inheritance of £87 to sail to South Africa to solve a murder - as you would! After several scrapes on board, she arrives in South Africa, has several more scrapes before travelling to the Victoria Falls where she has several more scra</span>
  <span id="freeText6182875393021558930" style="display:none">What a hoot this is! It’s so melodramatic and the storyline is quite absurd but it was just what I needed to lighten my mood. Anne Beddingfeld is a pompous, self righteous, impressionable and bored young woman. Having lost her father recently, she spends her entire inheritance of £87 to sail to South Africa to solve a murder - as you would! After several scrapes on board, she arrives in South Africa, has several more scrapes before travelling to the Victoria Falls where she has several more scrapes. The final denouement takes place in Johannesburg where the Rand Rebellion is just starting. From a historical point of view, that was certainly interesting.<br /><br />This really is just nonsense but very entertaining. I laughed aloud frequently and don’t regret reading it at all. 3 stars because it’s really not a very good book!</span>

<div id="review_2794982737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794982737" />
    <a title="Ed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1077703-ed"><img alt="Ed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442473851p2/1077703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1077703-ed?shelf=ed-s_cozy_mysteries_read">ed-s_cozy_mysteries_read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2794982737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12804021980105297373">Anne Beddingfield is a young lady who strikes off in pursuit of adventures, and she's rewarded in spades. I like the romance theme, but the mystery is the best part. Agatha Christie's prose style is amazing in places. The African setting was probably more exotic in her day, but it's interesting to see how Anne gets along while she's away from England. All in all, I enjoyed reading this book. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_594502211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/594502211" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6022914-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421168922p2/6022914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/594502211?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/6022914-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062074379" href="/book/show/12034587-the-man-in-the-brown-suit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6022914-james?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6022914-james?shelf=i-own-paperback">i-own-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6022914-james?shelf=i-own-ebook">i-own-ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer594502211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11985177163472274665">Sometimes it's easy to get distracted reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a>. You get used to the idea that she's the creator of Poirot, of Marple, even of Tommy and Tuppence. Those characters can almost become more important than the novel itself, and when you read a Christie that doesn't have the distraction of a famous detective creation you can be surprised by just how good Christie can be. To be fair, those other novels with Poirot in are pretty good too but this one struck me that I was just enjoying <i>
  </i></span>
  <span id="freeText11985177163472274665" style="display:none">Sometimes it's easy to get distracted reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>. You get used to the idea that she's the creator of Poirot, of Marple, even of Tommy and Tuppence. Those characters can almost become more important than the novel itself, and when you read a Christie that doesn't have the distraction of a famous detective creation you can be surprised by just how good Christie can be. To be fair, those other novels with Poirot in are pretty good too but this one struck me that I was just enjoying <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12034587.The_Man_in_the_Brown_Suit__Colonel_Race___1_" title="The Man in the Brown Suit (Colonel Race, #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Man in the Brown Suit</a>
</i> on it's own single-novel merits than with say a Poirot where I'm in part enjoying revisiting the characters she's created.<br /><br />Anne Beddingfield is a woman of spirit. When she witnesses a man falling in front of a train on the Underground she suspects there's more to what, at first glance, appears to be just a tragic accident. Before we know it, she's into full-on adventuress mode and booking cruises and train journeys and chasing down various suspects. At various times she suspects pretty much everybody in the cast of course, so we're left none the wiser. You assume Colonel Race is in the clear – in part because Anne suspects him too much but mostly because he goes on to appear in a couple of later Poirots as a supporting character (although, this is Christie, even that doesn't give him a free pass) – and Mrs. Blair who seems to be having far too much fun helping Anne to be the baddy. Anne's narrative is interspersed with extracts from Sir Eustace's diary, which is a clever idea allowing Christie to provide extra information outside of Anne's direct experience.<br /><br />All the characters – apart from Colonel Race – appear to be exaggerated for comedic effect. Anne is super spunky; Mrs. Blair is the rich widow (although she's still married she spends so much time apart from her husband she may as well be) who wants to adopt Anne; Sir Eustace is a somewhat pervy older bachelor writing his memoirs; the put upon suspect of the police – the titular man in the brown suit – is rugged, handsome and difficult, etc. and so on. They're mostly silly, but not too overdone. Characters get to appear and disappear in various disguises, even changing gender, and everybody is fooled. But it works, like Superman and his glasses. As a final cherry on the top, the novel features a nicely clever bit of unreliable narration which I always enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11985177163472274665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<div id="review_2785286953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2785286953" />
    <a title="Alexandra Elend Wolf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48780241-alexandra-elend-wolf"><img alt="Alexandra Elend Wolf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587677046p2/48780241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2785286953?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra Elend Wolf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra Elend Wolf" href="/user/show/48780241-alexandra-elend-wolf">Alexandra Elend Wolf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17183908-the-man-in-the-brown-suit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48780241-alexandra-elend-wolf?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48780241-alexandra-elend-wolf?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2785286953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4517308718708455481"><i> <b> "I felt alone in a wonderful world. Wrapped in a strange peace, I stood there, taking no heed of time, lost in a dream." </b> </i><br/><br/>I had quite forgotten how amazing Christie's writing truly is.<br/><br/>Though at the beginning I was more than a bit lost as to where Christie wanted to get with all that rather... <i> out of place </i> narration of the most mundane things and the lack of Colonel Race, which I had well-founded suspicions had to appear <b> sometime </b> seeing as how he gives name to this particular series of myst</span>
  <span id="freeText4517308718708455481" style="display:none"><i> <b> "I felt alone in a wonderful world. Wrapped in a strange peace, I stood there, taking no heed of time, lost in a dream." </b> </i><br /><br />I had quite forgotten how amazing Christie's writing truly is.<br /><br />Though at the beginning I was more than a bit lost as to where Christie wanted to get with all that rather... <i> out of place </i> narration of the most mundane things and the lack of Colonel Race, which I had well-founded suspicions had to appear <b> sometime </b> seeing as how he gives name to this particular series of mysteries, and instead we had a completely different narrator, it picked pace soon enough.<br /><br />Yes, the beginning was dull. Mostly because it wasn't what I was expecting from a mystery novel, it soon introduced us to our mystery and was nice to have all the facts that, later on, would play rather important parts in the story and solving the mystery at hand.<br /><br /><i> <b> "She was one of these energetic young women who are in love with life, and have not the faintest intention of quitting it." </b> </i><br /><br />Our main protagonists Anne Beddingfeld is a strong, witty, independent and a rather stubborn girl who is <i> determined </i> to have adventures and <i> enjoy </i> of her youth, even though she doesn't have much money and it's not particularly the most sensible thing to do. <br /><br />She was rather charming as a narrator pulsing life and determination through every sentence regardless of whatever situation that was currently occurring. She managed to make a compelling story.<br /><br />The other assortment of characters was, well, mysterious which is, I believe, the exact feeling you must achieve when writing a mystery. <br /><br />It is quickly established that one of these persons is our culprit the whole questions is <i> who? </i><br /><br />I was thoroughly deceived. Even though I was most clearly warned to not let my senses deceive me. I do think is very clever the way Christie put that one. Obvious yet unexpected and rather sneaky. <br /><br /><i> <b> "The opinion of other people never interested him in the slightest degree. I think it was really a sign of his greatness." </b> </i><br /><br />I don't really know how to review this kind of books without revealing anything and aside from what I've already said I believe there's little else to add. <br /><br />Maybe that I really liked Colonel Race and I want to continue following his career. That I'm, clearly, reading more book from this author, which is something I've been meaning to do for <i> ages </i> but I'll really start now. <br /><br />And, well, just that the whole experience is wonderful and close to my heart since, after all, Agatha Christie was the writer that sparked my interested in reading and the first author I ever read. <br /><br /><i> <b> "He was a thoroughgoing villain, I daresay – but he was a pleasant one. I’ve never met anyone half so amusing since." </b> </i><br />_________________________<br /><br />Ahh, such a good book. <br /><br />So satisfying. <br /><br />RTC. <br />__________________________<br /><br />It's been a long time coming for me to get around to reading another Agatha Christie book. The two I've read I loved so much and I don't know why it took me so long to get around to doing it.<br /><br />I'm starting here with Colonel Race's series because that's the one I enjoyed the most.<br /><br />Obviously, since it's a mystery, I'm going into this one without knowing <i> anything </i> about it and I'm just ready to let this book surprise me and blow me away. <br /><br />I just love classics. I wish I read them more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4517308718708455481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15625739274017571257">Another wonderful story. I also liked the way Christie intermingled Anne’s narrative with the use of the unreliable "narrator" in the extracts from Sir Eustace Pedler's diary. <br/><br/>Anne the heroine’s father has suddenly died and she finds herself relying on the kindness of friends.   <span id="freeText15625739274017571257" style="display:none">Another wonderful story. I also liked the way Christie intermingled Anne’s narrative with the use of the unreliable "narrator" in the extracts from Sir Eustace Pedler's diary. <br /><br />Anne the heroine’s father has suddenly died and she finds herself relying on the kindness of friends. She comes to London looking for adventure when she sees a man fall to his death on the live rails at Hyde Park tube station. Before he falls he has a terrified look on his face and turning round Anne sees a man in a brown suit. He announces he is a doctor declares the man is dead. So begins Anne’s adventures. <br /><br />She finds a scrap of paper dropped by the man saying 1 7.1 22 Kilmorden. Then a second murder takes place where a young woman is found strangled at Mill House, the home of Sir Eustace Pedler, MP. Anne decides to investigate and the evidence takes her on board the Kilmorden Castle sailing to Cape Town.<br /><br />The ship has several characters. She is befriended by Mrs Suzanne Sinclair a wealthy socialite, Colonel Race a spy for the government, Sir Eustace Pedler MP, his two secretaries the sinister Pagett and the mysterious Harry Rayburn as well as a suspicious clergyman Mr Chichester. One of these is the mastermind criminal known as the Colonel. <br /><br />She then has a series of adventures where she survives, diamonds are involved and she finds romance. A novel with murder and international intrigue with the setting in England, a ship voyage and South Africa. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_851254631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851254631" />
    <a title="C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10501026-c"><img alt="C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578542204p2/10501026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/851254631?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="C." href="/user/show/10501026-c">C.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440052302" href="/book/show/13414700-the-man-in-the-brown-suit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10501026-c?shelf=riedel-titles-2014">riedel-titles-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer851254631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6367543141573663624">I savour <b>Agatha Christie</b> in order of her releases. I don’t identify ahead what pertains to which series, nor watch any films lest I be wholly surprised by my journey; 90 years after “<b>The Man In The Brown Suit</b>”, came out. The gift this gives me is that each time I open the front page, it is a treat to discover which heroes shall escort me. <b>Agatha</b> experimented with these first four; three are unrelated. This one has nothing to do with her two famous sleuths. I was blissfully unprepared for that su</span>
  <span id="freeText6367543141573663624" style="display:none">I savour <b>Agatha Christie</b> in order of her releases. I don’t identify ahead what pertains to which series, nor watch any films lest I be wholly surprised by my journey; 90 years after “<b>The Man In The Brown Suit</b>”, came out. The gift this gives me is that each time I open the front page, it is a treat to discover which heroes shall escort me. <b>Agatha</b> experimented with these first four; three are unrelated. This one has nothing to do with her two famous sleuths. I was blissfully unprepared for that surprise.<br /><br />We move briskly, set formulaic traditions askew, and I many times chuckled in my bed. When I reviewed <i>“The Mysterious Affair At Styles”</i> I was stunned by <b>Agatha’s</b> plotting and exquisite language but not in love with that cast. I gave 3 stars, saving room for novels to rate higher. Here is a 5! The daughter of a single-minded palaeontologist is freed from caring for him and witnesses an accident that wasn’t investigated properly. Bolstered by her keenness at filling in the blanks, she willingly follows the case aboard a ship; creating one of the most fantastic novels I have ever read. I adored every page!<br /><br />Running around Africa on the strength of wild intellect, deft disguises, old and new crimes culminating, Kimberly diamonds, and even romance. The hilarious dialogues between <i>‘Anne’</i> and her shipmates create a successful book as it is. I adore <i>Suzanne Blair</i> as much as <i>Anne</i>. What makes it extraordinary is its peculiar flow. There are no weak personalities. <i>Anne &amp; Suzanne</i> thrive on every intrigue, with resolve we believe. The shifts and twists are smooth. The oddest thing is, the ladies deduce a great deal very early. With trivialities settled aboard ship; one imagines the adventuring in Africa can only be grand!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6367543141573663624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_714447350" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/714447350" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/714447350?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11958111-the-man-in-the-brown-suit">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer714447350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13899309297262090626">This is one of Agatha Christie's best stand alone novels - part mystery, part thriller and part espionage story - which takes us from a London tube station to revolution in Africa. It begins with Anne Beddingfeld, the daughter of a professor who longs for adventure. She spends her day trying to placate creditors and longing to 'step out' with a young man. When her father dies, she takes an opportunity to go to London, where, quite by chance, she witnesses the death of a young man at a tube stati</span>
  <span id="freeText13899309297262090626" style="display:none">This is one of Agatha Christie's best stand alone novels - part mystery, part thriller and part espionage story - which takes us from a London tube station to revolution in Africa. It begins with Anne Beddingfeld, the daughter of a professor who longs for adventure. She spends her day trying to placate creditors and longing to 'step out' with a young man. When her father dies, she takes an opportunity to go to London, where, quite by chance, she witnesses the death of a young man at a tube station. Finding a piece of paper dropped by the 'doctor' at the scene, she believes the death to be linked to that of the murder of a young woman at the house of Sir Eustace Pedlar. With only eighty five pounds to her name, her deductions ignored by the police, she boards a ship bound for South Africa. On board she meets not only Sir Eustace Pedlar but his secretary Guy Pagett, the society beauty Suzanne Blair, the enigmatic Colonel Race and the attractive Harry Rayburn. If she can find out who the man in the brown suit is, seen leaving Sir Pedlar's house shortly after the murder, she hopes for a job on the Daily Budget and life as a journalist.<br /><br />What follows is more of an adventure than the enterprising Anne could ever have dreamed of when she was tucked away in the quiet countryside. Some of the people Anne meets are certainly not who they appear to be and, before events have sorted themselves out, she will be kidnapped, nearly murdered (more than once!), face criminal gangs, find love and unearth the mysterious 'Colonel'. An excellent introduction to Christie if you haven't tried her books before. Sit back, relax and let the best mystery writer who ever put pen to paper take you on an adventure... </span>
  <a data-text-id="13899309297262090626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7455810944674308734" style="display:none">Despite the glaringly large amounts of misogyny spouted by numerous characters, including main character Anne (where it was most totally unpalatable and wince-inducing), this was a pretty funny story of an international criminal organization, a diamond heist, a plucky heroine, men in disguises, frustrating secretaries, and murder, of course.<br />Anne is refreshingly clear on what she wants and wants to do, and sets herself on a plan to figure out who the man in the brown suit is. <span id="freeTextContainer2461202453243098069">Read the full review at <a href='https://elgeewrites.com/review-shots-christie-murder-mysteries-links-secret-chimneys-man-brown-suit/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elgee Writes</a><br/><br/>In The Man in the Brown Suit we have a new lead detective Anne Beddingfeld. Anne leaves the country in search of a new adventure after her famous father dies. Soon enough she witnesses an accidental death and she finds a clue that might have something to do with death. She throws caution to the wind and decides to chase the clues that may prove it was not just another accident.<br/><br/>Her journey takes her to Africa and further on the trail of the murderer.   <span id="freeText2461202453243098069" style="display:none">Read the full review at <a href="https://elgeewrites.com/review-shots-christie-murder-mysteries-links-secret-chimneys-man-brown-suit/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Elgee Writes</a><br /><br />In The Man in the Brown Suit we have a new lead detective Anne Beddingfeld. Anne leaves the country in search of a new adventure after her famous father dies. Soon enough she witnesses an accidental death and she finds a clue that might have something to do with death. She throws caution to the wind and decides to chase the clues that may prove it was not just another accident.<br /><br />Her journey takes her to Africa and further on the trail of the murderer. Anne forms new friends, saves a stranger and makes stronger enemies. But does she make friends with the right person? How far will her sense of adventure take? You need to read The Man in the Brown Suit to know if the murderer was caught and who was the mastermind behind it all.<br /><br />My thoughts<br />Christie has a bunch of recurring detective characters but Anne Beddingfeld appears only in The Man in the Brown Suit. I didn’t like her at all, and I can say she was too naive and annoying for my taste. Of course others might find her lively and perky compared to Tommy and Tuppence or even Poirot.<br /><br />Bottom line<br />I definitely didn’t solve the case, so that is a positive thing I guess. But it bored me during some parts and I was wishing it would end soon. <br /><br /><a href="https://elgeewrites.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/elgeewrites" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/elgeewrites" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.amazon.in/gp/profile/amzn1.account.AHHNMWLTU24FLIQ2ZKFJXAWCB42Q?ref_=cm_cr_srp_d_pdp&amp;" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Amazon</a> |</span>

<div id="review_1481696763" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1481696763" />
    <a title="Mir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/237469-mir"><img alt="Mir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275489063p2/237469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1481696763?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mir" href="/user/show/237469-mir">Mir</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/237469-mir?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1481696763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12960300959130311569">My library's copy of this is "adapted by Hughot"?!<br/><br/>---<br/><br/>Currently DNF at page 81.<br/>This was the most boring Christie I have encountered to date. I've already forgotten the name of the MC, a young woman who is both irritatingly girlish and almost sociopathically cold (which sounds interesting and could be, written differently, but I think we are supposed to find her sympathetic). Her father has just died, she doesn't care -- fine, he didn't care for her, either -- she's staying with some near stranger</span>
  <span id="freeText12960300959130311569" style="display:none">My library's copy of this is "adapted by Hughot"?!<br /><br />---<br /><br />Currently DNF at page 81.<br />This was the most boring Christie I have encountered to date. I've already forgotten the name of the MC, a young woman who is both irritatingly girlish and almost sociopathically cold (which sounds interesting and could be, written differently, but I think we are supposed to find her sympathetic). Her father has just died, she doesn't care -- fine, he didn't care for her, either -- she's staying with some near strangers who kindly took her in, she decided to investigate a murder because she thinks she can parlay it into a job with a newspaper or money to travel. <br /><br />That's all fine on paper, but I just didn't enjoy her narrative voice in the slightest. And because she doesn't care about the murder, neither do I as the reader. I got my hopes up briefly when we switched to Sir Eustace, but he is also extremely indifferent. Oh, some espionage? Maybe my secretary was poisoned? Such a nuisance, just want a quiet life, oh well, at least Africa has warm weather. <br /><br />Colonel Race has just appeared on the scene, don't know anything about him yet, but at this point don't care. I certainly don't care if the protagonists gets a love interest. I pity the fool!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12960300959130311569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7494549139866449729">I think it's SPOIL FREE lol<br/>I read Sparkling cyanide without knowing that this is the 1st in the Colonel Race's collection, nevertheless, It was an outstanding read, took me a deal of time to finish it as I had a sort of busy year in University, Anyways, there happened 2 murders in London, and the man in the brown suit was present in both of them, Anne was there so she suspected him and wanted to know who that person is, she had this gipsy adventurous mentality that urged her to follow him up to </span>
  <span id="freeText7494549139866449729" style="display:none">I think it's SPOIL FREE lol<br />I read Sparkling cyanide without knowing that this is the 1st in the Colonel Race's collection, nevertheless, It was an outstanding read, took me a deal of time to finish it as I had a sort of busy year in University, Anyways, there happened 2 murders in London, and the man in the brown suit was present in both of them, Anne was there so she suspected him and wanted to know who that person is, she had this gipsy adventurous mentality that urged her to follow him up to South Africa - where most of the events took place -. There was a long story after these 2 crimes and a very hazardous secret organisation behind them, so there happened a series of events in which she was almost murdered, not just once but 3 times, and she found out that her journey's companion to S.Africa was the head of this organisation where they call him the " Colonel ", and the man in the brown suit was just trying to clear his name off a diamonds' theft that happened years before ... <br />This is a must read !</span>
  <a data-text-id="7494549139866449729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60141417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1736548341761720735">This read very differently from the large majority of Christie's work - it sounded like a cross between Christie and Wodehouse. I laughed almost the entire way through, even if it was a bit too silly in parts. Loved it.</span>

          </span>
